29-July 1970
440
Contact Report on Alexander SANKO, on 28 July 1970.
1.
On the morning of 28 July, I called Sam to check in with him
after being away on TOY for almost 6 weeks. He sounded a bit
upset at not being contacted during this period, so I dashed
out to his Hollywood home to explain what had happened and set
him at ease.
2.
It was plain to see that the trip had changed him. He is now
a bit presumptory, cocky, and know it all James Bond. He told
the other people who stories about being tailed in Madrid "by
7 or 8 'Chivatos" (Castellero, and Gasi, leading them on long
"8 or 9 mile hikes through Madrid," Caine agents were also
"watching" him on the day he was in Barcelona and on the short
layover his Pan Am plane had in Lisbon on his "a" home. At no
time, however, was he molested by these "agents"
3.
The Castro surveillance continued -so Sam says- in Hollywood.
"About the second night after I got home," c. 14-15 June, a car
began, was a great deal and a little to the rear of his'house
"after it got dark." He got into his car and went to the
gas station, the car -described the "barn" like a white Volkswagen,
without headlights on - followed San's car. on his short trip in
the neighborhood and back to his home. He could not make out
the physical description of the driver of the car. He went
up.
4.
The only other suspicious individual near his home, was "new
thin man," (described as about 5-11 to 6 ft and 170 lbs; Black
hair; no distinguishing features visible; once wearing slacks and
white shirt, another time wearing a suit). This individual showed
up across the street from his home "just as the sun had gone down,
several evenings during the first week that I got home. (c. 14-18
June) The man just walked past the front back and forth a few times
and departed to have his car around the corner of Sam's house. He
could have the car or anything else about the man.
5.
Again, during the last year, he was in the San received several
telephone calls where no one would answer when the phone was picked
up, or the person calling would say, "sorry where" Sam
has not experienced any other suspicious incidents after the first
week home from Spain. I should note that Sam does not talk of back
these incidents with fear, but ratherin the vein of the person was
referred to by the other.
6.
Sam would admit that he enjoyed himself somewhat in Madrid as
a tourist, although he did not deny that he stayed in luxury hotel,
ate as well as drank well, saw the sites and even went to night
club, all on the house. He went so far as to say that if he had
"known it was going to be like this, I never would have gone." Yet,
in the same breath, he told "Milliam" that he would be back in
Spain in September. of course, Sam would go again if we asked him,

2
But, only to help by country." (With "Patriots" like Sam, how
can we lose.)
7.
Sam is most anxious to start some correspondence to "William."
He says. "William" asked him to send him some photos of Capo Kennedy
to the smoked shrimp. Sam wants to know if we want to supply
him with the capo that he can send. Sam states he will
write anything we wish. I promised to check out the status of the
case with my office and David to see what course of action they
deen should be initiated.
8.
Modesty not being one of his greatest virtues Sam rabbled and
rambled about the "secrets" he got out of "William" and passed
on to the Madrid c/o. I went along with him and complimented him
to the Wall' dona; which is true. But, he was not satisfied with
my plaudits. He was a man now "that Washington said?" To which I
said, "everyone, Washington, and the Miami thought you did an
cealient job and we are most grateful for our cooperation." He
liked that very much; you could see it in the world. He
he tries to make it sound like it was a great ordeal and sacrifice
on his part to go to Spain to see "William," but he cannot hide
the way to get on the next plane to Madrid, and the good life there.
9.
I pointed out that "William" is now back in Cuba and there is no
indication of the most important return. Nevertheless, Sam feels he
should write him "because I matter will be sent to Cuba to him."
I assured him that I would get attending on thin matter and have
an answer for him sometime next week at that time, I promised to
take him and his close friend Nasp to him. Sam gave me an
extensive and expensive expense account of his trip. I will attempt
to make the idea of this report.
10. We ended the meeting. Every cordial terms. He was not so mad at
not being contacted so much as we were dying to get back on the gravy
train, and so much time has passed by the world to or from
"William." Sam asked for some way in which he was.
"right away" if "william" notifies him "that he's ready to jump.
He said, "I have won't have much time." I pointed out
that at present will be in Cuba and the prospects of him
defecting from Cuba right now, we very slim indeed. We would, however,
take this into consideration after the "William" returns to Spain or
another foreign post. We will be seeing each other next week to
clear up the accounting, (we owe him money, he says) and have lunch.
Henry S. PACHANKIS.

Name:
Orestes Guillermo RUIZ Perez
DROB:
10 February 1930, Havana Municipal District, Havana
Province
Occupation:
Minister, Cuban Charge d' affaires in Spain. From
August 1964 until late 1967, he was Vice-Minister of
the Ministry of Foreign Trade (MINCEX) From 1 August
1963 until mid-1964, he was Cuban Commercial Counsellor
in Mexico. From 1959 until 1962, he was an official
executive officer of the Ministry of Foreign Trade (MINCEX)
and 1962 as Director of Economy Financing of the Minis-
try of Treasury. It has also been reported that he
was a G-2 member (member of the Department of State
Security (DSE)) in 1961 and 1962. It has been reported
that he had been working at the Ministry of Treasury
since prior to 1958, that is, under the Details re-
gina. So far, we have not been able to confirm this
information.
Date of arrival
at post:
Exact date unknown. We believe that he has been hold-
ing his present position since at least 18 November 1967.
Physical
description: White, approximately 5'7" tall, about 180 pounds of
weight (it has been reported that he has a stout build),
light-colored eyes (blue or green), blond hair (some-
what way and combed back), round face. Has no visible
identification marks.
Parents:
a. Jose Antonio RUIZ (the matronymic is probably Armas)
b. Nieves PEREZ Entrialog.
C. RUIZ

Nilda VECIANA López, born between 1934 and 1942, place

Drother of Guillermo RUIZ Paroz. White, born approximately
in 1930. He is working as a farm laboror, waiting for his
turn to depart Cuba by way of Spain. Married, opposed to
the ragimo. Rosidos in the City of Havana Source: Dobrio-
ing of Manuel Domingo German VIGOS Peros, 24 Feb 70, I-122.
J. CARDOSO Perez, Rolando:
OTA-1858, 16. Jan 70, I-33. Dobriefing of Rolando CARDOSO
Poroz. Traces on this person.
K. VIGOS Perez, Manuel Domingo German:
VIGOS Perez, Manuel Domingo:
Al8: 780 716. DPOB: 5/12/41, Havana, Cuba. U.S. address:
4000 NW Fourth t., Miami, Fla. Address in Cuba: 353 San-
tos Suarez St., Santos Suarez, Havana. Entered the U.S.
at Miami on 2/20/70 (RD-1065). No occupation in Cuba.
Single. Source: Immigration card.
VIGOS Perez, Manuel D.:
Trip Varadero-Miami, 20 Feb 70. He is 28 years old. Has
no passport. Bricklayer. Source: AIRLIFT passenger list.
L. BORGES Dobarros, Mercedes:
Resides in Miami, Fla. Sister of Jorge BORGES Dobarros
(homosexual). (BORGES is a close friend of Source). Source:
Debriefing of Manuel Domingo VIGOS Perez, 24 Feb 70, I-122.
GARCIA Dobarros, Mercedes:
Rosidos at 4000 NW Fourth St., Miami, Fla., where Source,
who is a friend of hers, is residing. Source: Dobriefing
of Manuel Domingo German VIGOS Perez, 24 Feb 70, I-122.
M. GOMEZ Lemus, Antonio:
Head of the Department of Associations of the Havana Pro-
visional Revolutionary Government. Interventor o" the Ha-
vana Association of Veterans. Handed it over to Liberation
Army Lt. Antonio PANUCIA Garcia. Source: Press, 10/15/60.
Attended the "Condecoration of Drivers" which was hold in
the Declaration of Havana Hall of the Provisional Government.
Source: Press, 11/18/60.
Has a college degree. Greated the "Cobre Agrarian Star"
and her companions when they visited Havana. Source:
Press, 1/7/61.
Official of the Havana Provisional Government. Communist

N. BORGES Dobarros, Jorge:
Hemosexual and close friend of source. The latter rosided
in his house when he arrived in the U.S. Born approximately
in 1923. Prior to 1963, he worked with Mucbleria Salas
Furniture Store as an interior decorator and also as a
salesman. Worked with the MICONS (Ministry of Construction),
in Havana, as a watchman at construction work sites. Sources:
Dobricfing of Manual Domingo German VIGOS Pares, 24 Feb 70,
I-122:
BORGES Dobarros, Jorge B.:
Trip Varadoro-Miami, 20 Feb 70. 46 years old. Cuban pass-
port PP-026677. Employee. Source: AIRLIFT passenger list.
BORGES Dobarros, Jorge Benito:
A18 781 146. DP0B: 4/19/23, Havana, Cuba. U.S. address:

at Miami on 2/20/70 (RD-1065). Passport PP-026677, issued
on 4/9/69. Single. Source: Immigration card.
